            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">MDPI AG</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  As an emerging energy storage technol., Na-CO2 batteries with high energy d. are drawing tremendous attention because of their advantages of combining cost-effective energy conversion and storage with CO2 clean recycle and utilization.  Nevertheless, their com. applications are impeded by unsatisfactory electrochem. performance including large overpotentials, poor rate capability, fast capacity deterioration, and inferior durability, which mainly results from the inefficient electrocatalysts of cathode materials.  Therefore, novel structured cathode materials with efficient catalytic activity are highly desired.  In this review, the latest advances of catalytic cathode materials for Na-CO2 batteries are summarized, with a special emphasis on the electrocatalysts for CO2 redn. and evolution, the formation and decompn. of discharge product, as well as their catalytic mechanism.  Finally, an outlook is also proposed for the future development of Na-CO2 batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr56BsaXJVvorVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lio2kcH5D9boQ"> &gt;&gt;                 10.1016/j.joule.2021.02.004</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D5%26publication_year%3D2021%26pages%3D975-997%26journal%3DJoule%26author%3DZ.%2BZhuo%26author%3DK.%2BDai%26author%3DR.%2BQiao%26author%3DR.%2BWang%26author%3DJ.%2BWu%26author%3DY.%2BLiu%26author%3DJ.%2BPeng%26author%3DL.%2BChen%26author%3DY.-d.%2BChuang%26author%3DF.%2BPan%26author%3DZ.-x.%2BShen%26author%3DG.%2BLiu%26author%3DH.%2BLi%26author%3DT.%2BP.%2BDevereaux%26author%3DW.%2BYang%26title%3DCycling%2BMechanism%2Bof%2BLi2MnO3%253A%2BLi-CO2%2BBatteries%2Band%2BCommonality%2Bon%2BOxygen%2BRedox%2Bin%2BCathode%2BMaterials%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.joule.2021.02.004&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.1c14334&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.joule.2021.02.004&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit2R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">2</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Cycling mechanism of Li2MnO3: Li-CO2 batteries and commonality on oxygen redox in cathode materials</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhuo, Zengqing; Dai, Kehua; Qiao, Ruimin; Wang, Rui; Wu, Jinpeng; Liu, Yali; Peng, Jiayue; Chen, Liquan; Chuang, Yi-de; Pan, Feng; Shen, Zhi-xun; Liu, Gao; Li, Hong; Devereaux, Thomas P.; Yang, Wanli</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Joule</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">975-997</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JOULBR</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2542-4351</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Cell Press</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Li2MnO3 has been considered to be a representative Li-rich compd. with active debates on oxygen activities.  Here, by evaluating the Mn and O states in the bulk and on the surface of Li2MnO3, we clarify that Mn(III/IV) redox dominates the reversible bulk redox in Li2MnO3, while the initial charge plateau is from surface reactions with oxygen release and carbonate decompn.  No lattice oxygen redox is involved at any electrochem. stage.  The carbonate formation and decompn. indicate the catalytic property of the Li2MnO3 surface, which inspires Li-CO2/air batteries with Li2MnO3 acting as a superior electrocatalyst.  The absence of lattice oxygen redox in Li2MnO3 questions the origin of the oxygen redox in Li-rich compds., which is found to be of the same nature as that in conventional materials based on spectroscopic comparisons.  These findings provide guidelines on understanding and controlling oxygen activities toward high-energy cathodes and suggest opportunities on using alkali-rich materials for catalytic reactions.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpSg3o7jyvSH7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgYeGZlMUaeDQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXlvVais7o%253D&amp;md5=021f4b709afab9876eeb4247f7548720</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref3'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit3" data-doi="10.1038/s41467-020-15355-0"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Manthiram, A.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Reflection on Lithium-Ion Battery Cathode Chemistry</span>. <i>Nat.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Abstr.: Lithium-ion batteries have aided the portable electronics revolution for nearly three decades.  They are now enabling vehicle electrification and beginning to enter the utility industry.  The emergence and dominance of lithium-ion batteries are due to their higher energy d. compared to other rechargeable battery systems, enabled by the design and development of high-energy d. electrode materials.  Basic science research, involving solid-state chem. and physics, has been at the center of this endeavor, particularly during the 1970s and 1980s.  With the award of the 2019 Nobel Prize in Chem. to the development of lithium-ion batteries, it is enlightening to look back at the evolution of the cathode chem. that made the modern lithium-ion technol. feasible.  This review article provides a reflection on how fundamental studies have facilitated the discovery, optimization, and rational design of three major categories of oxide cathodes for lithium-ion batteries, and a personal perspective on the future of this important area.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpMra5MR0oCsrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgYeGZlMUaeDQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXlvFGnu78%253D&amp;md5=b22ad36cb85609ef702f570cf096eef0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref4'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit4" data-doi="10.1126/sciadv.aas9820"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lin, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pei, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cui, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Materials for Lithium-Ion Battery Safety</span>. <i>Sci.                         cas_cit5R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">5</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A comprehensive review of sodium layered oxides: powerful cathodes for Na-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Han, Man Huon; Gonzalo, Elena; Singh, Gurpreet; Rojo, Teofilo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The room temp. Na-ion secondary battery has been under focus lately due to its feasibility to compete against the already well-established Li-ion secondary battery.  Although there are many obstacles to overcome before the Na-ion battery becomes com. available, recent research discoveries corroborate that some of the cathode materials for the Na-ion battery have indeed indisputable advantages over its Li-ion counterparts.  In this publication, a comprehensive review of layered oxides (NaTMO2, TM = Ti, V, Cr, Mn, Fe, Co, Ni, and a mixt. of 2 or 3 elements) as a viable Na-ion battery cathode is presented.  Single TM systems are well characterized not only for their electrochem. performance but also for their structural transitions during the cycle.  Binary TM systems are investigated in order to address issues regarding low reversible capacity, capacity retention, operating voltage, and structural stability.  As a consequence, some materials already have reached an energy d. of 520 mW h g-1, which is comparable to that of LiFePO4.  Furthermore, some ternary TM systems retained more than 72% of their capacity along with over 99.7% Coulombic efficiency for 275 cycles.  The goal of this review is to present the development of Na layered oxide materials in the past as well as the state of the art today in order to emphasize the compatibility and durability of layered oxides as powerful candidates for Na-ion battery cathode materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpwo96Ash7WNbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgYeGZlMUaeDQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXitVCrsLjE&amp;md5=d938be66a2a0948e3d2f589b803dbf76</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref6'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit6" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201410376"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kundu, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Talaie, E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Duffort, V.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nazar, L.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review. However, the electrochem. performance of sodium-ion full cells (SIFCs) suffers severely from the irreversible consumption of sodium ions of cathode during the solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) formation of hard carbon anode.  Here, a high-efficiency cathode sodiation compensation reagent, sodium oxalate (Na2C2O4), which possesses both a high theor. capacity of 400 mA h g-1 and a capacity utilization as high as 99%, is proposed.  The implementation of Na2C2O4 as sacrificial sodium species is successfully realized by decreasing its oxidn. potential from 4.41 to 3.97 V through tuning conductive additives with different physicochem. features, and the corresponding mechanism of oxidn. potential manipulation is analyzed.  Electrochem. results show that in the full cell based on a hard carbon anode and a P2-Na2/3Ni1/3Mn1/3Ti1/3O2 cathode with Na2C2O4 as a sodium reservoir to compensate for sodium loss during SEI formation, the capacity retention is increased from 63% to 85% after 200 cycles and the energy d. is improved from 129.2 to 172.6 W h kg-1.  This work can provide a new avenue for accelerating the development of SIFCs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoXfx3ggjViUrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljBSeYxcNLvUQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhtlajsLfL&amp;md5=efa33ceb1fed7e592acc16b3afabcd21</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref10"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref10'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">10</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit10" data-doi="10.1016/j.carbon.2019.10.015"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shan, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guan, H.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Argueta, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, X.-L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, D.-S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Austin, D.                 10.1016/j.carbon.2019.10.015</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D157%26publication_year%3D2020%26pages%3D308-315%26journal%3DCarbon%26author%3DC.%2BShan%26author%3DX.%2BFeng%26author%3DJ.%2BYang%26author%3DX.%2BYang%26author%3DH.-Y.%2BGuan%26author%3DM.%2BArgueta%26author%3DX.-L.%2BWu%26author%3DD.-S.%2BLiu%26author%3DD.%2BJ.%2BAustin%26author%3DP.%2BNie%26author%3DY.%2BYue%26title%3DHierarchical%2BPorous%2BCarbon%2BPellicles%253A%2BElectrospinning%2BSynthesis%2Band%2BApplications%2Bas%2BAnodes%2Bfor%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%2Bwith%2Ban%2BOutstanding%2BPerformance%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.carbon.2019.10.015&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.1c14334&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.carbon.2019.10.015&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit10R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">10</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hierarchical porous carbon pellicles: Electrospinning synthesis and applications as anodes for sodium-ion batteries with an outstanding performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Shan, Changsheng; Feng, Xi; Yang, Jingxuan; Yang, Xu; Guan, Hong-Yu; Argueta, Monica; Wu, Xing-Long; Liu, Dao-Sheng; Austin, Douglas J.; Nie, Ping; Yue, Yanfeng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">157</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">308-315</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CRBNAH</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0008-6223</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">N-doped hierarchically structured carbon pellicles (CZIF-8/PAN) were prepd. from the carbonization of zeolitic imidazolate framework (ZIF-8)/polyacrylonitrile (PAN) composite fibers which were fabricated by electrospinning technique.  The resultant free-standing nanofiberic pellicles can be cut into membrane disks and directly used as anode materials without any binder and additive.  As an anode for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), the CZIF-8/PAN nanofiberic carbon pellicles showed superior reversible capacities of 186.2 mAh g-1 at high c.d. of 1.0 A g-1 and an excellent cyclic stability (93.5% remaining after 600 cycles) compared to other similar reported carbonaceous anode materials for SIBs.  The improved electrochem. performance of CZIF-8/PAN carbon pellicles is mainly attributed to the hierarchical porous structures produced by introducing large ZIF-8 particles as a template, which greatly promotes the large sodium cation transportation and electron transfer rates due to the enlarged pores and increased contact area between the electrode and electrolyte.  In addn., the enhanced electrochem. performance of CZIF-8/PAN nanofiberic anodes also benefits from the doping of nitrogen atoms which enhance the cond. and increase the active sites.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqbHn9dgfPrC7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljBSeYxcNLvUQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXitVKnsrvF&amp;md5=1f7b84c3f20f9140a31aee025b9f82b5</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref11"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref11'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">11</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit11" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2016.08.096"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Meng, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xie, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiao, D.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Lithium and Sodium Storage in Highly Ordered Mesoporous Nitrogen-Doped Carbons Derived from Honey</span>. <i>J. Power Sources</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>335</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">20</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">30</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.jpowsour.2016.08.096</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D335%26publication_year%3D2016%26pages%3D20-30%26journal%3DJ.%2BPower%2BSources%26author%3DY.%2BZhang%26author%3DL.%2BChen%26author%3DY.%2BMeng%26author%3DJ.%2BXie%26author%3DY.%2BGuo%26author%3DD.%2BXiao%26title%3DLithium%2Band%2BSodium%2BStorage%2Bin%2BHighly%2BOrdered%2BMesoporous%2BNitrogen-Doped%2BCarbons%2BDerived%2Bfrom%2BHoney%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.jpowsour.2016.08.096&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.1c14334&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.jpowsour.2016.08.096&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit11R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">11</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Lithium and sodium storage in highly ordered mesoporous nitrogen-doped carbons derived from honey</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Yongzhi; Chen, Li; Meng, Yan; Xie, Jun; Guo, Yong; Xiao, Dan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">335</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">20-30</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Honey, a widely existent biomass, consists mainly of carbohydrate and other N-contg. substances such as proteins, enzymes and org. acids.  It can be mixed homogeneously with mesoporous SiO2 template for its excellent H2O-soly. and moderate viscosity.  Honey was employed as a N-contg. C precursor to prep. N-doped ordered mesoporous carbons (OMCs).  The obtained honey derived mesoporous N-doped carbons (HMNCs) with dilated interlayer spacings of 0.387-0.395 nm, narrow pore size distributions centering at ∼4 nm and satisfactory N contents of 1.38-4.32% offer superb dual functionality for Li-ion battery (LIB) and Na-ion battery (NIB) anodes.  Tested against Li, the optimized HMNC-700 delivers a superior reversible capacity of 1359 mA h g-1 after 10 cycles at 100 mA g-1 and excellent rate capability and cycling stability of 722 mA h g-1 after 200 cycles at 1 A g-1.  For NIB applications, HMNC-700 offers a high initial reversible capacity of 427 mA h g-1 and stable reversible capacity of 394 mA h g-1 at 100 mA g-1.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqvNRB77GZElLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljBSeYxcNLvUQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xhs1ynsL%252FK&amp;md5=585ff8172726bc23c6c5842cac7a7085</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref12'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit12" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201600377"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dai, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hitz, E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sprenkle, V. Mater. Interfaces</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>11</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">24164</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">24171</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acsami.9b07206</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D11%26publication_year%3D2019%26pages%3D24164-24171%26journal%3DACS%2BAppl.%2BMater.%2BInterfaces%26author%3DY.%2BLi%26author%3DJ.%2BHu%26author%3DZ.%2BWang%26author%3DK.%2BYang%26author%3DW.%2BHuang%26author%3DB.%2BCao%26author%3DZ.%2BLi%26author%3DW.%2BZhang%26author%3DF.%2BPan%26title%3DLow-Temperature%2BCatalytic%2BGraphitization%2Bto%2BEnhance%2BNa-Ion%2BTransportation%2Bin%2BCarbon%2BElectrodes%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facsami.9b07206&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.1c14334&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facsami.9b07206&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit14R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">14</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Low-Temperature Catalytic Graphitization to Enhance Na-Ion Transportation in Carbon Electrodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Yiwei; Hu, Jiangtao; Wang, Ziqi; Yang, Kai; Huang, Weiyuan; Cao, Bo; Li, Zhibo; Zhang, Wei; Pan, Feng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">27</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">24164-24171</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are now emerging as a low-cost alternative to the current lithium-ion batteries, but their performance is limited by the sluggish transportation of large Na ions in electrodes.  Expanded graphite has been employed in enhancing the transport kinetics.  However, high-performance graphite should be synthesized at high temps. when using traditional methods, which inevitably increases the total cost of material prodn.  To tackle the kinetic issue for SIBs, a three-dimensional network is developed of graphene during catalytic graphitization in carbon electrodes at a temp. as low as 450° by using Prussian blue as a precursor.  Furthermore, a strategy is proposed to enhance the transport ability of the Na-ion in the network by controlling the diffusion distance of the Fe cluster and the distance between Prussian blue particles, leading to optimized performance with both excellent high-rate performance (167 mAh g-1 at 1.0 A g-1) and high charging capacity (390 mAh g-1 at 0.05 A g-1).  The results provide insights into the engineering of ionic transport properties through low-temp. catalytic graphitization in electrodes for SIBs and help design high-performance and low-cost electrodes for large-scale energy storage systems.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrRqJn5YrYQaLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh9KisBrzH3RQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhtF2ks7nN&amp;md5=ae81623abefbf7f10d6522a2402d8270</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref15'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit15" data-doi="10.1039/C6TA04877C"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Y.-S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Waste Biomass Derived Hard Carbon as a High-Performance Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J. Mater. Chem. A</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>4</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">13046</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">13052</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A waste biomass derived hard carbon as a high-performance anode material for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Pin; Li, Yunming; Hu, Yong-Sheng; Li, Hong; Chen, Liquan; Huang, Xuejie</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">34</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">13046-13052</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The utilization of renewable energies has become increasingly urgent for the sustainable development of our society.  Energy storage systems are essential in order to efficiently use these energies.  Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) show bright prospect in the application for energy storage markets due to the potential low cost originating from unlimited sources and wide distribution of Na.  However, the anode remains a great challenge in the industrialization of SIBs.  Hard carbon holds the most promising future among all reported anodes; however, there are still two main shortcomings such as high cost and low initial coulombic efficiency, which limit its application.  Here, we report a hard carbon material derived from an abundant and abandoned biomass of corn cobs (HCC) using a simple carbonization method.  The HCC shows excellent sodium storage performance with a reversible capacity of ca. 300 mA h g-1, a high initial coulombic efficiency of 86% and good cycling stability.  A prototype sodium-ion battery was prepd. to prove the application prospect using HCC1300 as the anode and Na0.9[Cu0.22Fe0.30Mn0.48]O2 as the cathode, exhibiting a high energy d. of 207 W h kg-1 and a long cycle life.  These excellent properties demonstrate that HCC is a potential candidate as an anode material for sodium-ion battery application.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrzP3444VBrIbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh9KisBrzH3RQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xht1eju7nN&amp;md5=f6776d35bde5f3fb873f88fe495141b6</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref16"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref16'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">16</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit16" data-doi="10.1039/C8TA09750J"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Thompson, B.                         cas_cit16R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">16</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hierarchically structured composites and porous materials from soft templates: fabrication and applications</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Thompson, Benjamin R.; Horozov, Tommy S.; Stoyanov, Simeon. D.; Paunov, Vesselin N.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">14</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Recent exptl. methods for fabrication of hierarchically porous and structured composites are reviewed.  The main focus is on recent examples of how different soft templating materials, like emulsions, surfactant phases, breath figures, biol. templates, liq. marbles and hydrogel bead slurries can be used to fabricate hierarchically porous materials with tuneable porosity, pore sizes and ratios of different sized pores.  Approaches for tuning the phys. properties (mech., thermal, acoustic) of these innovative materials as well as controlling the porosity, pore size and microstructure are discussed.  We also show a variety of applications of hierarchically structured composites in catalysis, energy storage, usage and conversion, removal of pollutants, sensors, biomaterials, smart soaps, and structuring of consumer products.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpAewfbfDWRF7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh9KisBrzH3RQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXlslenurw%253D&amp;md5=48a9a06d761d4ca34024c80711d60e9a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref17"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref17'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">17</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit17" data-doi="10.1016/j.jechem.2020.06.031"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shao, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Weng, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jian, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Carbon Spheres with Rational Designed Surface and Secondary Particle-Piled Structures for Fast and Stable Sodium Storage</span>. <i>J.                 10.1016/j.jechem.2020.06.031</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D54%26publication_year%3D2021%26pages%3D368-376%26journal%3DJ.%2BEnergy%2BChem.%26author%3DW.%2BShao%26author%3DF.%2BHu%26author%3DS.%2BLiu%26author%3DT.%2BZhang%26author%3DC.%2BSong%26author%3DZ.%2BWeng%26author%3DJ.%2BWang%26author%3DX.%2BJian%26title%3DCarbon%2BSpheres%2Bwith%2BRational%2BDesigned%2BSurface%2Band%2BSecondary%2BParticle-Piled%2BStructures%2Bfor%2BFast%2Band%2BStable%2BSodium%2BStorage%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.jechem.2020.06.031&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.1c14334&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.jechem.2020.06.031&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Carbon spheres with rational designed surface and secondary particle-piled structures for fast and stable sodium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Shao, Wenlong; Hu, Fangyuan; Liu, Siyang; Zhang, Tianpeng; Song, Ce; Weng, Zhihuan; Wang, Jinyan; Jian, Xigao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Energy Chemistry</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">54</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">368-376</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JECOFG</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2095-4956</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Science Press</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The electrochem. performance of hard carbon in sodium storage is still limited by its poor cycling stability and rate capability because of the sluggish kinetics process.  In this study, we use a simple and effective method to accelerate the kinetics process by engineering the structure of the electrode to promote its surface and near-surface reactions.  This goal is realized by the use of slightly aggregated ultra-small carbon spheres.  The large sp. surface area formed by the small spheres can provide abundant active sites for electrochem. reactions.  The abundant mesopores and macropores derived from the secondary particle piled structure of the carbon spheres could facilitate the transport of electrolytes, shorten the diffusion distance of Na+ and accommodate the vol. expansion during cycling.  Benefiting from these unique structure features, PG700-3 (carbon spheres with the diams. of 40-60 nm carbonized at 700 °C) exhibits high performance for sodium storage.  A high reversible capacity of 163 mAh g-1 could be delivered at a c.d. of 1.0 A g-1 after 100 cycles.  Interestingly, at a c.d. of 10.0 A g-1, the specific capacity of PG700-3 gradually increases to 140 mAh g-1 after 10 000 cycles, corresponding to a capacity retention of 112%.  Given the enhanced kinetics of SIBs reactions, PG700-3 exhibits an excellent rate capability, i.e., 230 and 138 mAh g-1 at 0.1 and 5.0 A g-1, resp.  This study provides a facile method to attain high performance anode materials for SIBs.  The design strategy and improvement mechanism could be extended to other materials for high rate applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpPQqTQOv5iWLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh9KisBrzH3RQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XisFKqtbjK&amp;md5=0ec6733436a5ef5348caada473551d8a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref18'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit18" data-doi="10.1021/nl500970a"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fan, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jungjohann, K.                         cas_cit18R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">18</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">In Situ Transmission Electron Microscopy Study of Electrochemical Sodiation and Potassiation of Carbon Nanofibers</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Ying; Fan, Feifei; Wang, Jiangwei; Liu, Yang; Chen, Hailong; Jungjohann, Katherine L.; Xu, Yunhua; Zhu, Yujie; Bigio, David; Zhu, Ting; Wang, Chunsheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">14</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3445-3452</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NALEFD</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1530-6984</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Carbonaceous materials have great potential for applications as anodes of alkali-metal ion batteries, such as Na-ion batteries and K-ion batteries (NIB and KIBs).  We conduct an in situ study of the electrochem. driven sodiation and potassiation of individual carbon nanofibers (CNFs) by TEM.  The CNFs are hollow and consist of a bilayer wall with an outer layer of disordered-carbon (d-C) enclosing an inner layer of cryst.-carbon (c-C).  The d-C exhibits about three times vol. expansion of the c-C after full sodiation or potassiation, thus suggesting a much higher storage capacity of Na or K ions in d-C than c-C.  For the bilayer CNF-based electrode, a steady sodium capacity of 245 mAh/g is measured with a Coulombic efficiency approaching 98% after a few initial cycles.  The in situ TEM expts. also reveal the mech. degrdn. of CNFs through formation of longitudinal cracks near the c-C/d-C interface during sodiation and potassiation.  Geometrical changes of the tube are explained by a chemomech. model using the anisotropic sodiation/potassiation strains in c-C and d-C.  Our results provide mechanistic insights into the electrochem. reaction, microstructure evolution and mech. degrdn. of carbon-based anodes during sodiation and potassiation, shedding light onto the development of carbon-based electrodes for NIBs and KIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpRi8vSMVLHc7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgyRb82m_CyRg"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit19R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">19</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Commercial activated carbon as a novel precursor of the amorphous carbon for high-performance sodium-ion batteries anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Qi; Zhu, Youyu; Zhao, Pinyi; Yuan, Chao; Chen, Mingming; Wang, Chengyang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">129</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">85-94</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CRBNAH</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0008-6223</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Amorphous C-based anode materials are considered as one of the most promising candidates for Na-ion batteries (SIBs).  However, there are 2 main barriers before large-scale industrialization, i.e. low initial coulombic efficiency (ICE) and high cost caused by low C yield of precursors.  The authors report a novel com. activated amorphous C-based anode synthesized through a facile-tailored strategy consisting of annealing and surface coating.  The as-prepd. amorphous C has a porous internal structure but a low sp. surface area (SSA) with a dense surface C layer.  As an anode material for SIBs, the obtained amorphous C displays an outstanding electrochem. performance including a high reversible capacity of 391 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 25 mA g-1 with a high ICE of 80%, and a superior cycling performance with a capacity retention of 97% after 100 cycles.  The high ICE is mainly attributed to the denser surface C layer which suppresses the penetration of electrolyte and fully uses the internal porosity.  The com. availability, and the desirable properties make this novel amorphous C-based anode a promising candidate for SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp6WUwGYNDTqLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgyRb82m_CyRg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhvFKmt7nO&amp;md5=bc79d2a6f3a2ee36dd401ff6f93b4103</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref20"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref20'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">20</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit20" data-doi="10.1039/C4TA05451B"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Y.-S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Amorphous Monodispersed Hard Carbon Micro-Spherules Derived from Biomass as a High Performance Negative Electrode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit20R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">20</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Amorphous monodispersed hard carbon micro-spherules derived from biomass as a high performance negative electrode material for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Yunming; Xu, Shuyin; Wu, Xiaoyan; Yu, Juezhi; Wang, Yuesheng; Hu, Yong-Sheng; Li, Hong; Chen, Liquan; Huang, Xuejie</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are expected to be a promising com. alternative to lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) for large-scale and low-cost elec. energy storage applications in the near future.  Despite this, the absence of a suitable neg. electrode material hinders their development.  In this contribution, the authors synthesized monodispersed hard carbon spherules (HCS) from an abundant biomass of sucrose, and studied the influence of the carbonization temp. on the microstructure and electrochem. performance.  The initial coulombic efficiency of the HCS was increased to 83% by coating its surface with soft carbon through the pyrolysis of toluene.  The plateau capacity at the low potential region increased with increasing carbonization temp.  The HCS carbonized at 1600° showed the highest plateau capacity (220 mA-h/g) and excellent cycling performance with a capacity retention of 93% after 100 cycles.  When coupled with an air-stable P2-Na2/3Ni1/3Mn2/3O2 pos. electrode, the full cell exhibited a high initial coulombic efficiency of 76%, a mean operating voltage of 3.5 V and excellent cycling performance.  The theor. energy d. of this system is 200 W-h/kg.  These promising properties are believed to be close to the level required for practical applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo1jsHJQCoWPrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgyRb82m_CyRg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhvVSqs7bK&amp;md5=1d0ab49c7539719d3b644ebc28a2d568</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref21"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref21'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">21</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit21" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.8b15274"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bai, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Marriage of an Ether-Based Electrolyte with Hard Carbon Anodes Creates Superior Sodium-Ion Batteries with High Mass Loading</span>. <i>Acs Appl.                         cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Marriage of an Ether-Based Electrolyte with Hard Carbon Anodes Creates Superior Sodium-Ion Batteries with High Mass Loading</span></div><div class="casAuthors">He, Yongwu; Bai, Panxing; Gao, Shuyan; Xu, Yunhua</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">48</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Inferior rate performance, insufficient cycle life, and low mass loading have restricted the practical application of hard C (HC) anodes in Na-ion batteries (NIBs).  Here, a compatible strategy is developed by matching HC anodes with an ether-based electrolyte.  A systematic study reveals that good compatibility of the electrode-electrolyte systems forms thinner but a more sustainable solid-electrolyte interphase and delivers a higher ionic cond. and Na+ ion diffusion coeff. than the commonly used ester-based electrolytes.  Therefore, an excellent electrochem. performance is demonstrated with a long cycle life (∼196 mAh/g and 90% capacity retention after 2000 cycles at 1 A/g), a super rate capability (∼51% capacity retention at 10 A/g) at a mass loading of 1.5 mg/cm2, and a high initial Coulombic efficiency of 85.9%.  A high reversible areal capacity of 4.3 mAh/cm2 can be achieved at an ultrahigh mass loading of 17 mg/cm2, superior to all reported HC anodes.  Our findings not only shed light on the design of high-performance battery systems but also promise a com. transformation from the lab. test to mass prodn. of NIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrBl0ltiwR75bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgyRb82m_CyRg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXitFWmu7rI&amp;md5=840c025e787c6f6eaeda77e95bf38325</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref22'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit22" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2018.02.002"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bai, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiong, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Long Cycle Life and High Rate Sodium-Ion Chemistry for Hard Carbon Anodes</span>. <i>Energy Storage Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>13</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">274</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">282</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Manipulating Electrode/Electrolyte Interphases of Sodium-Ion Batteries: Strategies and Perspectives</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Enhui; Niu, Yubin; Yin, Ya-Xia; Guo, Yu-Guo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Materials Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">18-41</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AMLCEF</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2639-4979</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  After the past decade's rapid development, the com. demands for sodium ion batteries (SIBs) have been put on the schedule for large-scale energy storage.  Even though the electrode-electrolyte interphases play a very important role in detg. the overall battery performance in terms of high energy d. and long-cycling stability, studies regarding their fundamental understanding and regulation strategies are still in their infancy.  Herein, we comprehensively review the current research status and the challenging issues of the as-generated SIB interphases from three main aspects.  Firstly, a fundamental understanding of the main body interphase layers is introduced through the development of their formation mechanism, their compn./structure, and the dynamic evolution process involved, all of which are highly responsible for the Na+ ion transport behavior to det. the final kinetic diffusion.  Then, interphase manipulation via the parental electrolyte is summarized in terms of electrolyte engineering strategies, such as the solvent/salt selection, the concn. effect, and the functional additive screening to build a more stable interphase layer for desirable electrochem. reversibility.  Finally, potential effects from the chosen electrodes are discussed to provide necessary assocns. with the interphase formation and evolution.  Crit. challenges for building stable Na-based interphase are identified, and in particular, new ways of thinking about the interphase chem. and the electrolyte chem. based on SIBs, are strongly appealing.  We believe that this work is likely to attract attention to the rational design of Na-based interphase layers towards high-energy and long-life-span batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqVuJ3ZWCnEX7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgyRb82m_CyRg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXisVWntb3J&amp;md5=5cc0e78592ac0fc5cb0e24007ba54fa6</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit24" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201702724"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Goktas, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bolli, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Berg, E.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard carbon is considered as the most prospective anode material for sodium ion batteries.  However, the loss of plateau capacities at high rates, arising from large electrochem. polarization, causes rapid degrdn. in the rate performances of batteries.                         cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Achieving superb sodium storage performance on carbon anodes through an ether-derived solid electrolyte interphase</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Jun; Wang, Da-Wei; Lv, Wei; Zhang, Siwei; Liang, Qinghua; Zheng, Dequn; Kang, Feiyu; Yang, Quan-Hong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">370-376</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">High sp. surface area carbon (HSSAC) is a class of promising high-capacity anode materials for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  A crit. bottleneck of the HSSAC anode, however, is the ultra-low initial coulombic efficiency (ICE) in commonly used ester-based electrolytes.  This phenomenon further prohibits improving the specific capacity, long-term stability and rate capability of HSSAC anodes.  This work reports the largely enhanced anode performance of several different HSSAC anodes in ether-based electrolytes.  Very importantly, with the reduced graphene oxide (rGO) anode as one example, the ICE can be as high as 74.6% accompanied by a large reversible specific capacity of 509 mA h g-1 after 100 cycles at a c.d. of 0.1 A g-1. 75.2% of the capacity was retained after 1000 cycles at 1 A g-1.  Even at a high c.d. of 5 A g-1, the specific capacity of the rGO anode can be obtained at 196 mA h g-1.  This extraordinary performance is ascribed to the stable, thin, compact, uniform and ion conducting solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) formed in an ether-based electrolyte.  Fortunately, this SEI-modifying strategy is generic and is independent of the specific microstructures of HSSAC anodes, indicating a promising avenue for manipulating the SEI on HSSAC anodes through utilizing ether solvents to enable achievement of high ICE for large-capacity HSSAC anodes for practical applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq2QXpPrjk4ZbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljHp9CuWPopQQ"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Breaking the limitation of sodium-ion storage for nanostructured carbon anode by engineering desolvation barrier with neat electrolytes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhen, Yichao; Sa, Rongjian; Zhou, Kaiqiang; Ding, Lingyi; Chen, Yang; Mathur, Sanjay; Hong, Zhensheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">74</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">In the past, most of the studies monotonously focused on developing electrode materials for sodium ion batteries (SIBs), while the compatibility effects and mechanism of electrolytes with material microstructures on the sodiation behavior are barely involved.  Here, we demonstrate the sodium-ion storage behavior of carbon anode in neat ether electrolytes with outstanding ion diffusion kinetics at electrode surface that breaks its innate limitation.  Porous nanocarbon with small interlayer spacing but very high surface area exhibits a record high ICE over 91.1% and exceptional rate capability for Na-ion storage in ether-based electrolytes.  This is due to the remarkably reduced Na+ desolvation barrier in ether electrolytes (~ 94.6 meV) that is less than one-third of that in ester electrolytes (~ 307.8 meV).  The strong interaction of Na-ions with ester electrolytes and their decompn. on electrode surface can be suppressed by adopting ether solvents owing to lower Gibbs free energies of solvation and Na+ desolvation energy as revealed by DFT calcns.  For electrode materials working with ether electrolytes, a large surface area is crit. for better electrochem. performance.  This study provides a reliable regulation parameter for tailoring electrolytes with materials that offers promising potential for nanostructured materials toward high-rate rechargeable devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqS0TD-28deDrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljHp9CuWPopQQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXpsl2lurk%253D&amp;md5=f2d67c236a462110626b9cf64945f75c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit28" data-doi="10.1002/celc.201600365"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dahbi, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nakano, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yabuuchi, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fujimura, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chihara, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kubota, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Son, J.                         cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Effect of Hexafluorophosphate and Fluoroethylene Carbonate on Electrochemical Performance and Surface Layer of Hard Carbon for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Dahbi, Mouad; Nakano, Takeshi; Yabuuchi, Naoaki; Fujimura, Shun; Chihara, Kuniko; Son, Jin-Young; Cui, Yi-Tao; Oji, Hiroshi; Komaba, Shinichi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ChemElectroChem</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Electrochem. sodium insertion for hard carbon is examd. in a cyclic alkylene carbonate-based soln. contg. sodium perchlorate (NaClO4) or sodium hexafluorophosphate (NaPF6) salt with fluoroethylene carbonate (FEC) additive to study electrolyte dependency for Na-ion batteries.  NaPF6-based electrolytes provided superior reversibility and cyclability of sodium insertion into hard carbon compared to NaClO4-based ones.  The FEC-derived passivation film improves the capacity retention because of better passivation with a thinner surface layer, which is revealed by hard and soft XPS (PES).  Using both the NaPF6 salt and FEC additive results in a synergetic effect on passivation for the hard-carbon electrode, leading to enhanced cycle performance.  Hard-carbon electrodes with poly (vinylede difluoride) binder in propylene carbonate-based electrolytes contg. NaPF6 and FEC demonstrates the excellent capacity retention with reversible capacity of ca. 250 mAh g-1.  The difference in capacity retention for the electrolytes is expected to originate from a consequence of the difference in the surface interphase layer formed on the hard-carbon electrodes.                         cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Impact of the electrolyte salt anion on the solid electrolyte interphase formation in sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Eshetu, Gebrekidan Gebresilassie; Diemant, Thomas; Hekmatfar, Maral; Grugeon, Sylvie; Behm, R. Juergen; Laruelle, Stephane; Armand, Michel; Passerini, Stefano</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">55</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Aiming at a more comprehensive understanding of the solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) in sodium ion batteries (NIBs), a detailed XPS investigation of the few-nanometer thick passivation film formed on hard carbon (HC) in contact with various Na+-ion conducting electrolytes is reported.  The electrolytes investigated include 1 M solns. of NaPF6, NaClO4, NaTFSI, NaFSI, and NaFTFSI, all dissolved in a common mixt. of ethylene carbonate (EC) and diethylene carbonate (DEC) (EC/DEC = 1/1 wt. ratio).  For comparison, the study of analogous Li-based electrolytes contg. LiPF6 and LiFSI as representative electrolyte salts is also reported.  The anion and cation of the electrolyte salt appear to play a key role in detg. the overall SEI layer compn., including its depth evolution and thickness.  The SEI building species formed on hard carbon by solvent redn. upon sodiation are found to decrease with the various salts in the order: NaPF6 &gt; NaClO4 ≈ NaTFSI &gt; NaFTFSI &gt; NaFSI.  The comparison of lithiated and sodiated HC electrodes shows that the SEI layer is more homogeneous and richer in org. species upon the use of Na-based electrolytes.  Surface and depth-profiling XPS anal. on HC electrodes charged in the various electrolyte formulations provides in-depth insights on the differences and similarities of the SEI (compn., thickness, depth evolution, etc.) evolving from the variation in the chem. structure of the cations and anions of the resp. salts.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpLMSeL81S-cbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj_eFH3G454FA"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Surface capacitive contributions: Towards high rate anode materials for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Sheng; Qiu, Jingxia; Lai, Chao; Ling, Min; Zhao, Huijun; Zhang, Shanqing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">224-230</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NEANCA</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2211-2855</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Due to the poor transportability of sodium ions, conventional sodium ion batteries (SIBs) cannot deliver sufficient capacity for high rate applications.  Surface-induced capacitive processes (SCP) (e.g. capacitance and pseudocapacitance) could provide fast charge/discharge capacity in conjunction with the capacity provided by diffusion-controlled intercalation processes (DIP) to address this issue.  For the first time, SCP was used to design a hierarchical layered graphene composite as an anode material for high rate SIBs.  The contributions of the individual sodium storage processes were quant. evaluated, verifying the proposed mechanism.  The resultant SCP-enhanced SIB delivers an outstanding rate capacity of 120 mAh/g at 10 A/g, which is among best of the state-of-the-art carbon-based SIBs.  It also demonstrates exceptional cycling stability, retaining 83.5% capacity of 142 mAh/g at 0.5 A/g after 2500 cycles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpbh0np0PgmXLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj_eFH3G454FA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXovVSksA%253D%253D&amp;md5=74a639e183cc3ff6dd8d427fd201e54e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref31"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref31'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">31</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit31" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201801361"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, D.-W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lv, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qin, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Niu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kang, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, Q.-H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Ethers Illume Sodium-Based Battery Chemistry: Uniqueness, Surprise, and Challenges</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Partially Single-Crystalline Mesoporous Nb2O5 Nanosheets in between Graphene for Ultrafast Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Liu; Bi, Xiaofang; Yang, Shubin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>

                        cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-Performance Sodium-Ion Pseudocapacitors Based on Hierarchically Porous Nanowire Composites</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Zheng; Augustyn, Veronica; Jia, Xilai; Xiao, Qiangfeng; Dunn, Bruce; Lu, Yunfeng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2012</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4319-4327</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Elec. energy storage plays an increasingly important role in modern society.  Current energy storage methods are highly dependent on lithium-ion energy storage devices, and the expanded use of these technologies is likely to affect existing lithium reserves.  The abundance of sodium makes Na-ion-based devices attractive as an alternative, sustainable energy storage system.  However, electrodes based on transition-metal oxides often show slow kinetics and poor cycling stability, limiting their use as Na-ion-based energy storage devices.  The present paper details a new direction for electrode architectures for Na-ion storage.  Using a simple hydrothermal process, we synthesized interpenetrating porous networks consisting of layer-structured V2O5 nanowires and carbon nanotubes (CNTs).  This type of architecture provides facile sodium insertion/extn. and fast electron transfer, enabling the fabrication of high-performance Na-ion pseudocapacitors with an org. electrolyte.  Hybrid asym. capacitors incorporating the V2O5/CNT nanowire composites as the anode operated at a max. voltage of 2.8 V and delivered a max. energy of ∼40 Wh kg-1, which is comparable to Li-ion-based asym. capacitors.  The availability of capacitive storage based on Na-ion systems is an attractive, cost-effective alternative to Li-ion systems.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrumiwdbkvAg7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj_eFH3G454FA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XkvFOntrk%253D&amp;md5=25ac2558f28dfdc865bedb7315709124</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref34'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit34" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201702434"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">3D Amorphous Carbon with Controlled Porous and Disordered Structures as a High-Rate Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Metal-free hybrid seawater fuel cell with an ether-based electrolyte</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Hyojin; Park, Jeong-Sun; Sahgong, Sun Hye; Park, Sangmin; Kim, Jae-Kwang; Kim, Youngsik</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
